Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|01|<h2>Basic &gt; Automatic<a name="Basic_Automatic"></a></h2>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|02|<blockquote>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|03|<h3>Automatic</h3>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|05|<p>This probe checks whether the device responds to SNMP. If it doesn't, the probe is set to Ping/Echo.</p>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|06|<p><b>How it works:</b></p>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|07|<p>InterMapper sends a SNMP GetNextRequest for the sysName, sysObjectID, and sysServices OIDs (1.3.6.1.2.1.1.5.5, 1.3.6.1.2.1.1.5.2, and 1.3.6.1.2.1.1.5.7, respectively) using the specified SNMP Read-only community string. Upon receiving a valid SNMP response, InterMapper sets the device's probe to SNMP. If not, the Ping/Echo probe is used.</p>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|08|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|09|<p>None.</p>
Basic/Automatic|com.dartware.automatic|10|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.automatic</span><br />

Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|03|<h3>SQL Server Query</h3>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|05|<p>This probe establishes an ADO (ActiveX Data Object) connection to a Microsoft SQL Server running on the target host.  It issues the specified query and displays the returned fields.  If no records are returned, the device status is set to <i>Critical</i>.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|07|<p><i>Query</i> - contains the SQL query to send. It should be enclosed in double-quotes. Using the "TOP" keyword in your query improve the response to the query. You may want to specify specific columns in your query and include a "WHERE" or an "ORDER BY" clause.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|08|<p><i>Rows</i> and <i>Columns</i> - let you limit the output of your query. Enter the number of "Columns" and the number of "Rows" records of the query you want to view.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|09|<p><i>Instance</i> - specifies the SQL Server instance on the target host the query is sent to. If you wish to query the default server instance, leave this field blank.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|10|<p><i>Database</i> - specifies the database on the target instance to query.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|11|<p><i>User</i> - can be an SQL Server user on the target host, or may take the form of "domain&#92;user" for a domain login. Leave it blank to use integrated authentication.  The specified user must have dbreader privileges to the database.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|12|<p><i>Timeout (sec)</i> - allows you to override the device's specified timeout.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|13|<p>InterMapper invokes the sql_query.vbs script, included with this probe.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Microsoft/SQL Server Query|com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt|14|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.cmd.sql_query.txt</span><br />

Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; DHCPv4/BOOTP<a name="Servers_Standard_DHCPv4_BOOTP"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|03|<h3>DHCPv4/BOOTP</h3>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|05|<p>DHCP is the protocol used by IP clients to obtain an IPv4 address and other parameters for using TCP/IP. Depending on your setup, this probe may work only if your computer is already using an IP address acquired using BOOTP or DHCP.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|06|<p><b>Note:</b> On Mac OS X, this probe will only work if no DHCP, Bootp, or PPP interfaces are enabled.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|07|<p>The  probe sends DHCP-INFORM requests to test the DHCP mechanism for an IP subnet.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|08|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|09|<p><i>BOOTP Relay Address</i> - the IP address to which all DHCP requests are addressed. Normal BOOTP/DHCP requests are broadcast to the local subnet (255.255.255.255), where they are picked up by the BOOTP agent in a router and relayed to the BOOTP/DHCP server. If this parameter is left blank, InterMapper sends the DHCP requests directly to the device's IP address.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|10|<p><i>DHCP Client ID</i> - an optional parameter included with the DHCP-INFORM request that can be used to identify the DHCP client as InterMapper. If this parameter is blank, InterMapper does not include the DHCP Client ID option in its DHCP probe.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|11|<p><i>DHCP Subnet Mask</i> - an optional parameter that specifies the expected value of the subnet mask returned by the DHCP server. If this parameter is blank, InterMapper accepts any subnet mask value.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|12|<p><i>DHCP Router Address</i> - an optional parameter that specifies the expected value of the router address returned by the DHCP server. If this parameter is blank, InterMapper accepts any router address value.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|13|<p><i>DHCP Message Type</i> - the type of DHCP message to send. Typically, you should use DHCP-INFORM, since this type will not cause the DHCP server to allocate an IP address. A DHCP server may respond to a DHCP-DISCOVER request by leasing an IP address which will never be used.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|14|<p><i>Hardware Address</i> - an optional parameter that specifies the MAC address of the network interface used to send the DHCP request.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|15|<p><i>Request Seconds</i> - an optional parameter that specifies the number of seconds to claim we have been sending DHCP requests. Certain DHCP servers (such as the one supplied with OS X 10.5 with the default settings) do not respond until the client claims to have been trying for at least 10 seconds.</p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|16|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.dhcp</span><br />
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|17|Version:  <span class="code">2.1</span></p>
Servers-Standard/DHCPv4\/BOOTP|com.dartware.dhcp|18|<p><a href="Servers_Standard.htm">Back to Top</a></p>

Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Domain Name (DNS) &gt; DNS: (A) Address<a name="Servers_Standard_Domain_Name__DNS__DNS:__A__Address"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|03|<h3>DNS: (A) Address</h3>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|05|<p>DNS is the protocol used by TCP/IP network clients to translate Internet names into IP addresses, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1034.txt">RFC 1034</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1035.txt">RFC 1035</a>. This probe sends a DNS request to look up the IP address for a specified domain name.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|07|<p><i>Domain Name</i> - the fully qualified domain name you are attempting to resolve.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|08|<p><i>IP Address</i> - optional parameter specifies an IP address the domain name should resolve to. If this parameter is not blank, InterMapper reports the status specified in <i>Failure Status</i> if one of the returned IP addresses doesn't match this address.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|09|<p><i>Recursion Desired</i> - If the target DNS server cannot resolve the given domain name, and this parameter is <b>True</b>, the DNS server may query an authoritative DNS server. To prevent this behavior, use the default setting of <b>False</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|10|<p><i>Failure Status</i> - the device status InterMapper should report when the IP address in a DNS response doesn't match the specified <i>IP Address</i> parameter. By default, an IP address mismatch sets the device to Alarm. (Down is reserved for complete lack of response by the DNS server.)</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (A) Address|com.dartware.dns|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.dns</span><br />

Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Domain Name (DNS) &gt; DNS: (MX) Mail Server<a name="Servers_Standard_Domain_Name__DNS__DNS:__MX__Mail_Server"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|03|<h3>DNS: (MX) Mail Server</h3>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|05|<p>The protocol used by TCP/IP network clients to translate Internet names into Mail servers, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1034.txt">RFC 1034</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1035.txt">RFC 1035</a>. This probe sends a DNS request to look up the mail server for a specified domain name.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|07|<p><i>Domain Name</i> - the fully qualified domain name to be resolved.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|08|<p><i>Mail Server</i> - optional - specify a mail server the domain name should resolve to. If this parameter is non-empty, and one of the returned mail servers doesn't match the one provided, a status as specified in <i>Failure Status</i> is returned.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|09|<p><i>Recursion Desired</i> - If the target DNS server cannot resolve the given domain name, and this parameter is <b>True</b>, the DNS server may query an authoritative DNS server. To prevent this behavior, use the default setting of <b>False</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|10|<p><i>Failure Status</i> - specifies the device status returned when the DNS response returns a mail server that doesn't match the specified <i>Mail Server</i>. You can choose <b>Down</b>, <b>Alarm</b> or <b>Warning</b>. By default, mail server mismatches return an <b>Alarm</b> condition; <b>Down</b> is reserved for when the DNS server fails to respond at all.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (MX) Mail Server|com.dartware.dns.mx|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.dns.mx</span><br />

Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|03|<h3>DNS: (NS) Name Server</h3>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|05|<p>The protocol used by TCP/IP network clients to translate Internet names into name servers, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1034.txt">RFC 1034</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1035.txt">RFC 1035</a>. This probe sends a DNS request to look up the name server for a specified domain name. CNAME records are accepted if no NS records are present in the response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|07|<p><i>Domain Name</i> - the fully qualified domain name to be resolved.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|08|<p><i>Name Server</i> - optional - specify the name server the domain name should resolve to. If this parameter is non-empty, and one of the returned name servers doesn't match the one provided, a status as specified in <i>Failure Status</i> is returned. </p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|09|<p><i>Recursion Desired</i> - If the target DNS server cannot resolve the given domain name, and this parameter is <b>True</b>, the DNS server may query an authoritative DNS server. To prevent this behavior, use the default setting of <b>False</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (NS) Name Server|com.dartware.dns.ns|10|<p><i>Failure Status</i> - specifies the device status returned when the DNS response returns a name server that doesn't match the specified <i>Name Server</i>. You can choose <b>Down</b>, <b>Alarm</b> or <b>Warning</b>. By default, name server mismatches return an <b>Alarm</b> condition; <b>Down</b> is reserved for when the DNS server fails to respond at all.</p>

Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Domain Name (DNS) &gt; DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup<a name="Servers_Standard_Domain_Name__DNS__DNS:__PTR__Reverse_Lookup"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|03|<h3>DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup</h3>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|05|<p>The protocol used by TCP/IP network clients to translate IP addresses into Internet names, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1034.txt">RFC 1034</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1035.txt">RFC 1035</a>. This probe sends a DNS request to look up the domain name for a specified IP address. Both PTR and CNAME records are accepted in the response. </p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|07|<p><i>IP Address</i> - the fully qualified IP address to be resolved.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|08|<p><i>Domain Name</i> - optional - specify a domain name the IP address should resolve to. If this parameter is non-empty, and one of the returned domain names doesn't match the one provided, a status as specified in <i>Failure Status</i> is returned.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|09|<p><i>Recursion Desired</i> - If the target DNS server cannot resolve the given domain name, and this parameter is <b>True</b>, the DNS server may query an authoritative DNS server. To prevent this behavior, use the default setting of <b>False</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|10|<p><i>Failure Status</i> - specifies the device status returned when the DNS response returns a domain name that doesn't match the specified <i>Domain Name</i>. You can choose <b>Down</b>, <b>Alarm</b> or <b>Warning</b>. By default, mail server mismatches return an <b>Alarm</b> condition; <b>Down</b> is reserved for when the DNS server fails to respond at all.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.dns.ptr</span><br />
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|12|Version:  <span class="code">1.2</span></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|13|<p><a href="Servers_Standard.htm">Back to Top</a></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (PTR) Reverse Lookup|com.dartware.dns.ptr|14|</blockquote>

Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|03|<h3>DNS: (TXT) Text Record</h3>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|05|<p>The protocol used by TCP/IP network clients to translate Internet names into Text records, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1034.txt">RFC 1034</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1035.txt">RFC 1035</a>. This probe sends a DNS request to look up the text record for a specified domain name.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|07|<p><i>Domain Name</i> - the fully qualified domain name to be resolved.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|08|<p><i>Text Substring</i> - optional - specify a substring of a text record the domain name should resolve to. If this parameter is non-empty, and one of the returned text records doesn't contain the substring provided, the device's condition is set as specified in <i>Failure Status</i>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|09|<p><i>Recursion Desired</i> - If the target DNS server cannot resolve the given domain name, and this parameter is <b>True</b>, the DNS server may query an authoritative DNS server. To prevent this behavior, use the default setting of <b>False</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|10|<p><i>Failure Status</i> - specifies the device status returned when the DNS response text record in a DNS response doesn't contain the specified <i>Text Substring</i>. You can choose <b>Down</b>, <b>Alarm</b> or <b>Warning</b>. By default, mail server mismatches return an <b>Alarm</b> condition; <b>Down</b> is reserved for when the DNS server fails to respond at all. </p>
Servers-Standard/Domain Name (DNS)/DNS: (TXT) Text Record|com.dartware.dns.txt|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.dns.txt</span><br />

Servers-Standard/Mail/Roundtrip-IMAP|com.dartware.email.imap.txt|05|<p>This probe tests an IMAP server and measures the time it takes to send a message (via SMTP) and retrieve it (via IMAP). It sends a short message to the specified SMTP server, and continually attempts to retrieve the message via IMAP from the device being tested. The probe alerts if the server fails to respond properly or the round-trip time exceeds the specified timeout. </p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/Roundtrip-IMAP|com.dartware.email.imap.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>

Servers-Standard/Mail/Roundtrip-IMAP|com.dartware.email.imap.txt|11|<p><i>IMAP User</i> and <i>IMAP Password</i> - The user name and password used to log into the IMAP server to retrieve the message.</p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/Roundtrip-IMAP|com.dartware.email.imap.txt|12|<p><i>Timeout</i> - Measured in seconds.</p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/Roundtrip-IMAP|com.dartware.email.imap.txt|13|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.email.imap.txt</span><br />

Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|03|<h3>IPMI v2.0</h3>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|05|<p>This probe implements version 2.0 of the Intelligent Platform Management Interface (IPMI) over a LAN. It sends UDP-based RMCP+ packets to a Baseboard Management Controller (BMC) located within a server or workstation. The BMC is hardware which permits network-based management of the computer even when it is turned off, i.e. "lights-out management".</p>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|07|<p><i>User</i> - required - An administrator-level user name to the BMC.</p>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|08|<p><i>Password</i> - required - The password for the specified user.</p>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|09|<p><i>Dialect</i> - The variant of the IPMI protocol. There are subtle differences in implementations of IPMI in various products. </p>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|10|<li> To use this probe with an Apple XServe 2008 or earlier, set the "Dialect" parameter to "XServe". </li>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|11|<li> For Dell Servers, the Apple XServe 2009, and any other product set the "Dialect" parameter to "Other".</li>
Servers-Standard/IPMI v2.0|com.dartware.ipmi.txt|12|<p>This probe supports one-key, non-anonymous logins only. Internally, it uses RAKP-HMAC-SHA1 and AES-CBS-128 for authentication and confidentiality, respectively. The firewall configuration of the BMC must permit UDP packets from InterMapper.</p>

Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|00|<li><a href="Basic.htm#Basic_Ping_Echo">Basic &gt; Ping/Echo<MadCap:xref href="Basic.htm#Basic_Ping_Echo" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|01|<h2>Basic &gt; Ping/Echo<a name="Basic_Ping_Echo"></a></h2>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|02|<blockquote>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|03|<h3>Ping/Echo</h3>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|05|<p>This probe sends an ICMP echo request packet to the target device to determine if it is active and responding. </p>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|06|<p><b>Tip:</b> To send a 1500-byte IP packet to an IPv4 target, set the number of data bytes to 1472. To send the same IP packet size to an IPv6 target, set the number of data bytes to 1452.</p>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|07|<p>InterMapper sends the ping packet, then waits for a response. The device's specified Timeout value is used to determined the amount of time the probe waits for a response. If no response is received within the specified time, InterMapper re-sends the echo request, waiting again the device's Timeout. When the probe reaches the device's limit of the number of pings to send (as determined by the device or map's limit), without receiving a response, the device status is set to DOWN.</p>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|08|<p>By default, the number of echo requests is three, and the default timeout is three seconds. Thus it can take up to nine seconds to set a device status to DOWN.</p>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|09|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|10|<p><i>Number of Data Bytes</i> - The number of bytes of ICMP data to send. By default, 20 bytes of data is sent. The mimimum value is 16 bytes; the maximum is 2000 bytes.</p>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|11|<p><i>Data Pattern</i> - The hexadecimal pattern repeated throughout the payload contents.</p>
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|12|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.ping</span><br />
Basic/Ping\/Echo|com.dartware.ping|13|Version:  <span class="code">2.1</span></p>

Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|00|<li><a href="Servers_Standard.htm#Servers_Standard_RADIUS">Servers Standard &gt; RADIUS<MadCap:xref href="Servers_Standard.htm#Servers_Standard_RADIUS" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; RADIUS<a name="Servers_Standard_RADIUS"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|03|<h3>RADIUS</h3>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|05|<p>The protocol used by remote access servers to authenticate dial-in users, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2138.txt">RFC 2138</a>. This probe tests a RADIUS server by sending an Access-Request packet to authenticate a specific user name and password. Before you can use this probe with a particular RADIUS server, you must add the InterMapper computer's IP address to the RADIUS server and choose a "shared secret" for it. The "shared secret" is used by the RADIUS protocol to encrypt passwords in RADIUS requests. A RADIUS server does not answer access-requests from a client it doesn't recognize.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|06|<p>The official port number for RADIUS is 1812. Some RADIUS servers, however, use port number 1645 for historical reasons.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|08|<p><i>Shared Secret</i> - InterMapper's unique password into the RADIUS server. Since it is used for authentication, the same value must be configured in the RADIUS server as well.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|09|<p><i>User Name</i> - The user name to be used for InterMapper's authentication.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|10|<p><i>Password</i> - The password for the specified user name. The password is not sent in the clear; it is encrypted using the shared secret.</p>
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.radius</span><br />
Servers-Standard/RADIUS|com.dartware.radius|12|Version:  <span class="code">1.9</span></p>

This probe sends a SIP request in a single UDP packet and checks for a valid SIP response.</p>
Servers-Standard/SIP over UDP|com.dartware.sip.txt|06|<p>By default, this probe sends an OPTIONS command to the target device. However, some VOIP systems do not answer un-authenticated OPTIONS requests. For these devices, change the command to REGISTER.</p>

Basic/SNMP Traffic|com.dartware.snmp|05|<p>This probe retrieves system and traffic information from an SNMP-enabled device. This information comes from the system and interfaces groups of SNMP MIB-II. </p>
Basic/SNMP Traffic|com.dartware.snmp|06|<p>It shows traffic (bytes/second, packets/second, errors/minute) for each interface. Right-click a link to open the interface's Status Window. </p>
Basic/SNMP Traffic|com.dartware.snmp|07|<p>The probe also shows sysLocation, sysContact, and sysUptime from the system group in the device's Status Window.</p>
Basic/SNMP Traffic|com.dartware.snmp|08|<p><b>Note:</b> This is exactly the same probe as the "SNMP MIB-II" probe found in earlier versions of InterMapper. It was renamed to reflect its purpose more accurately.</p>

Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|01|<h2>Network Devices &gt; Cisco &gt; Cisco   Old CPU MIB<a name="Network_Devices_Cisco_Cisco___Old_CPU_MIB"></a></h2>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|02|<blockquote>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|03|<h3>Cisco - Old CPU MIB</h3>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|05|<p>This probe monitors the CPU and Memory utilization of a Cisco router.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|07|<p><i>CPU Busy - Alarm</i> - The ALARM threshold for CPU utilization in Per Cent. If the average CPU usage over a 1 minute interval exceeds this threshold, the device enters ALARM state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|08|<p><i>CPU Busy - Warning</i> - The WARNING threshold for CPU utilization in Per Cent. If the average CPU usage over a 1 minute interval exceeds this threshold, the device enters WARNING state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|09|<p><i>Low Memory - Alarm</i> - The ALARM threshold for the amount of free memory remaining (in bytes). If free memory drops below this threshold, the device enters ALARM state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Old CPU MIB|com.dartware.snmp.cisco|10|<p><i>Low Memory - Warning</i> - The WARNING threshold for the amount of free memory remaining (in bytes). If free memory drops below this threshold, the device enters WARNING state.</p>

Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|00|<li><a href="Network_Devices.htm#Network_Devices_Cisco_Cisco___IP_SLA_Jitter">Network Devices &gt; Cisco &gt; Cisco   IP SLA Jitter<MadCap:xref href="Network_Devices.htm#Network_Devices_Cisco_Cisco___IP_SLA_Jitter" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|01|<h2>Network Devices &gt; Cisco &gt; Cisco   IP SLA Jitter<a name="Network_Devices_Cisco_Cisco___IP_SLA_Jitter"></a></h2>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|02|<blockquote>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|03|<h3>Cisco - IP SLA Jitter</h3>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|05|<p>This probe extracts jitter test data from a Cisco IP SLA agent that is running on a Cisco router or switch. Typically these jitter tests are used to measure jitter, latency, and packet loss for VoIP and video conferencing applications.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|07|<p><i>SNMP Index</i> - The value used when configuring the IP SLA agent in the Cisco switch or router using the "ip sla monitor" command (see example below). This value identifies the jitter test, and is the SNMP index used by Intermapper to probe the device. To probe for different instances of jitter tests on a single Cisco switch or router, create separate devices on your Intermapper map, each using a different SNMP Index. </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|08|<p><i>Latency Alarm Threshold</i> - The ALARM threshold for latency in milliseconds. If Average Latency value exceeds this threshold, the device enters ALARM state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|09|<p><i>Latency Warning Threshold</i> The WARNING threshold for latency in milliseconds. If the Average Latency value exceeds this threshold, the device enters WARNING state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|10|<p><i>Jitter Alarm Threshold</i> - The ALARM threshold for Jitter. If the Average Jitter value exceeds this threshold, the device enters ALARM state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|11|<p><i>Jitter Warning Threshold</i> - The WARNING threshold for Jitter. If the Average Jitter value exceeds this threshold, the device enters WARNING state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|12|<p><i>Packet Loss Alarm Threshold</i> - The ALARM threshold for Packet Loss. If the Percent Packet Loss value exceeds this threshold, the device enters ALARM state.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|13|<p><b>Example</b></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|14|<p>Example IOS commands for configuring an IP SLA jitter test to run on a Cisco router or switch:</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|15|<p><span class="code">ip sla monitor 250</span></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|16|<p>  type jitter dest-ipaddr w.w.w.w dest-port 50505 source-ipaddr x.x.x.x num-packets 2000 interval 20</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|17|<p>  request-data-size 256 </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|18|<p>  owner yyyy</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|19|<p>  tag zzzz</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|20|<p>  exit</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|21|<p>In the above example specifies "250" as the SNMP index. This can be any value as long as it is unique. "w.w.w.w" is the IP address of the remote IP SLA responder. "x.x.x.x" is the local IP address of this IP SLA agent. "yyyy" is any text information identifying the owner of the test (e.g., name of network service provider). "zzzz" is any text information identifying this particular test.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|22|<p>To schedule the IP SLA test to run forever: </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|23|<p>ip sla monitor schedule 66 life forever start-time now</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|24|<p>To start the IP SLA responder on the remote IP SLA responder:</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|25|<p>  <span class="code">ip sla monitor responder</span></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|26|<p>In the above IOS commands, the jitter test does not specify a codec type, so ICPIF and MOS scores are not available. If the test is modified to include a codec type then minor revisions are required to this SNMP probe. Also, some routers and switches may not support the MIB variables for ICPIF and MOS scores - this depends on the IOS train. </p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|27|<p>More information about configuring Cisco IP SLA is available on the www.cisco.com site.</p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|28|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt</span><br />
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|29|Version:  <span class="code">2.4</span></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|30|<p><a href="Network_Devices.htm">Back to Top</a></p>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - IP SLA Jitter|com.dartware.snmp.cisco-ip-sla.txt|31|</blockquote>

Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Process and Memory Pool|com.dartware.snmp.cisconewmib|03|<h3>Cisco - Process and Memory Pool</h3>
Network Devices/Cisco/Cisco - Process and Memory Pool|com.dartware.snmp.cisconewmib|05|<p>This probe monitors the CPU and Memory utilization in a Cisco router. It uses variables from CISCO-MEMORY-POOL-MIB and CISCO-PROCESS-MIB.</p>

SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|03|<h3>String Comparison</h3>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|05|<p>This probe retrieves a single SNMP MIB variable, compares it to a specified value, and sets the device's severity based on the comparison. It also displays the value in the Status Window.</p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|07|<p><i>Variable</i> - the MIB name or OID to retrieve. If you have imported the MIB for this device, enter the symbolic name for this value. Otherwise, enter its OID. </p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|08|<p><i>Test</i> - choose whether the device is equal to the <i>Value</i> parameter or not. </p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|09|<p><i>Value</i> - the value to compare with the MIB variable's value.</p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|10|<p><i>Severity</i> - choose severity level to use if the value does not match the specified value.</p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|11|<p><i>Legend</i> - a text string used to identify the variable in the status window and in strip charts. If left blank, the variable's name or OID is used.</p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|12|<p><i>Units</i> - a text string displayed next to the variable's value in the Status Window. Usually used for units of measure (packets/sec, degrees, etc.) </p>
SNMP/String Comparison|com.dartware.snmp.oidstrcomparison.txt|13|<p><i>Tag</i> - A short text string that identifies a particular class of dataset. Tags are used to correlate different variables from different probes that describe the same type of data, such as CPU% or temperature.</p>

SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|01|<h2>SNMP &gt; Table Viewer<a name="SNMP_Table_Viewer"></a></h2>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|02|<blockquote>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|03|<h3>Table Viewer</h3>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|05|<p>This probe shows the contents of several useful tables from common SNMP MIBs. It retrieves its data by walking the SNMP data values in the tables.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|06|<li> <b>ifTable</b> - The "Interfaces" table gives information about the physical and logical interfaces of the device. It shows the following columns: <i>ifIndex</i>, <i>ifDescr</i>, <i>ifType</i>, <i>ifSpeed</i>, <i>ifPhysAddress</i>, <i>ifOperStatus</i>, and <i>ifAdminStatus</i>. It is defined in MIB-II (RFC-1213) and updated in the IF-MIB.</li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|07|<li> <b>ifXTable</b> - The "Extended Interfaces" table defined in IF-MIB. It adds the <i>ifName</i> and <i>ifAlias</i> fields/columns to those shown in <i>ifTable</i> above.</li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|08|<li> <b>Traffic Counters</b> - Shows traffic counters <i>ifInOctets</i> and <i>ifOutOctets</i> from the MIB-II ifTable, and the <i>ifHCInOctets</i> and <i>ifHCOutOctets</i> from the IF-MIB. To determine the traffic rate, refresh the window and compare two separate readings. The difference divided by the time between the refreshes (in seconds) is the number of bytes/second.</li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|09|<li> <b>tcpConnTable</b> - Shows information about any present connections: Variables include <i>tcpConnLocalAddress</i>, <i>tcpConnLocalPort</i>, <i>tcpConnRemAddress</i>, and <i>tcpConnRemPort</i>. It is defined in MIB-II.</li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|10|<li> <b>udpTable</b> - Shows information about any present UDP listeners: Variables include <i>udpLocalAddress</i>, <i>udpLocalPort</i>. It is defined in MIB-II.</li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|11|<li> <b>ipAddrTable</b> - Shows the IP address/mask/broadcast address for each interface. Includes <i>ipAdEntAddr</i>, <i>ipAdEntifIndex</i>, <i>ipAdEntNetMask</i>, <i>ipAdEntBcastAddr</i>,  and <i>ipAdEntReasmMaxSize</i>. It is defined in RFC-1213, and updated in the IP-MIB. </li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|12|<li> <b>ipRouteTable</b> - This table (currently deprecated) comes from RFC-1213 (MIB-II). </li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|13|<li> <b>ipCidrRouteTable</b> and <b>ipForwardTable</b> - These tables come from the IP-FORWARD-MIB, and show information about CIDR multi-path IP Routes. Note: the ipForwardTable obsoletes the ipRouteTable of MIB-II, and is in turn obsoleted by the ipCidrRouteTable.</li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|14|<li> <b>ipNetToMediaTable</b> - The "Net Address-to-Media Address" table (also known as the "ARP Table") shows these fields/columns: <i>ipNetToMediaIfIndex</i>, <i>ipNetToMediaNetAddress</i>, <i>ipNetToMediaPhysAddress</i>, and <i>ipNetToMediaType</i>. It is defined in RFC-1213.</li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|15|<li> <b>dot1dTpFdbTable</b> - The "Bridge MIB" (RFC1493) shows the forwarding database for transparent bridges. </li>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|16|<p>A link to each table appears in the Status Window. Click the link to see the contents of the table on the selected device.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|17|<p>This probe requires that you first import these MIBs: <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1213.txt">RFC1213-MIB (MIB-II)</a>, <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1493.txt">Bridge MIB (rfc1493)</a>, <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2011.txt">IP-MIB (rfc2011)</a>, <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2863.txt">IF-MIB (rfc2863)</a>, and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2096.txt">IP-FORWARD-MIB (rfc2096).</a> These are all bundled together in a <a href="http://intermapper.com/support/users/probes.html#tableviewer">single zip archive.</a> </p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|18|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|19|<p>None.</p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|20|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt</span><br />
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|21|Version:  <span class="code">1.9</span></p>
SNMP/Table Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.tableviewer.txt|22|<p><a href="SNMP.htm">Back to Top</a></p>

SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|01|<h2>SNMP &gt; Trap Viewer<a name="SNMP_Trap_Viewer"></a></h2>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|02|<blockquote>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|03|<h3>Trap Viewer</h3>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|05|<p>This probe listens for trap packets and displays the contents of a trap in the Status Window. It does not actively poll the device, and takes no action based on the contents of the trap. </p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|06|<p>All variables parsed from the trap packet appear in the device's Status Window. You can use this probe as a prototype for making your own trap probes.</p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|07|<p><b>How the Trap Viewer Probe Works</b></p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|08|<p>When a trap arrives, the probe parses the trap to retireve the values from the trap's header, along with the first ten items in its Varbind List. Each value is assigned to a variable for use by the probe; each is also shown in the Status Window.</p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|09|<p>To see how this probe works, you can configure your equipment to send traps to InterMapper, or use the net-snmp <b>snmptrap</b> command. Either way, the Status Window shows the values present in any traps that arrive.</p>
SNMP/Trap Viewer|com.dartware.snmp.trapdisplay.txt|10|<p>For more information on the <b>snmptrap</b> command, see the net-snmp documentation for the <a href="http://www.net-snmp.org/tutorial/tutorial-4/commands/snmptrap.html">trap tutorial</a> and the <a href="http://www.net-snmp.org/docs/man/snmpinform.html">snmptrap command</a>. Miscellaneous/Legacy/SNMP v2c|com.dartware.snmpv2c|05|<p>This is a legacy probe, provided for compatibility with InterMapper Traditional and older versions of InterMapper (&lt; 4.4). Use the SNMP MIB-II probe, setting the SNMP version to SNMP v2.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/SNMP v2c|com.dartware.snmpv2c|06|<p>The SNMP v2c probe retrieves MIB-II information from the device. This includes <i>sysLocation</i>, <i>sysContact</i>, and <i>sysUptime</i> from the system group, and traffic (bytes/second, packets/second, errors/minute) for each interface.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/SNMP v2c|com.dartware.snmpv2c|07|<p>It uses the 64-bit counters for interface traffic statistics. This provides accurate information (without rollover) on very high speed links.</p>

Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|08|<p><i>CPU Busy - Alarm</i> - specifies the <b>Alarm</b> threshold for CPU utilization as a percentage. If the average CPU usage over a 1 minute interval exceeds this threshold, the device is set to <i>Alarm</i> state.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|09|<p><i>CPU Busy - Warning</i> - specifies the <b>Warning</b> threshold for CPU utilization. If the average CPU usage over a 1 minute interval exceeds this threshold, the device is set to <i>Warning</i> state.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|10|<p><i>Low Memory - Alarm</i> - specifies the <b>Alarm</b> threshold for the amount of free memory remaining (in bytes). If the free memory drops below this threshold, the device is set to <i>Alarm</i> state.</p>
Miscellaneous/Legacy/Cisco (v2c)|com.dartware.snmpv2c.cisco|11|<p><i>Low Memory - Warning</i> - specifies the <b>Warning</b> threshold for the amount of free memory remaining (in bytes). If the free memory drops below this threshold, the device is set to <i>Warning</i> state.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|03|<h3></h3>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|05|<p>This probes monitors an Apache Web Server with the Apache Status module enabled (mod_status). The Apache Status module allows a server administrator to find out how well an Apache server is performing. This probe reads output of provided by the Status module that presents the current server statistics, using the <i>?auto</i> parameter.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|06|<p>To enable status reports for this probe, add this code to the httpd.conf file on the target server:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|07|<p><span class="code">  &lt;Location /server-status&gt;</span></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|08|<p>    SetHandler server-status</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|09|<p>    Order Deny,Allow</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|10|<p>    Deny from all</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|11|<p>    Allow from <i>InterMapper-Address</i></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|12|<p>  &lt;/Location&gt;</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|13|<p>  </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apache/|com.dartware.tcp.apache.txt|14|<p>This probe supports the Apache ExtendedStatus directive, if enabled.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|05|<p>This TCP probe queries a <a href="http://www.barracudanetworks.com/">Barracuda Spam Firewall</a> for various performance statistics.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|08|<p><i>User</i> - Firewall administrator name.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|09|<p><i>Password</i> - Firewall administrator password.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|10|<p><i>Port</i> - Firewall's Web Interface HTTP Port as set on the BASIC-&gt;Administration page.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|11|<p><b>Thresholds</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|12|<p>Set thresholds as follows:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|13|<p><i>In/Out Queue Size</i> - The returned value should normally be less than 100.  An In or Out Queue value that consistently exceeds 100 for more than 30 minutes <b><i>may</i></b>  indicate a problem that needs attention.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|14|<p><b>Note:</b> The returned value may rise temporarily, then go back down after 10 or 15 minutes. </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|15|<li> For the Inbound Queue, this is normal behavior, but can also be the result of an orchestrated attack.  The Barracuda attempts to read as many messages as it can, which results in a slower processing rate, which in turn increases the number of messages in the queue.  </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|16|<li> For the Outbound Queue, an increase usually indicates that the destination server is unavailable or the local DNS is not functioning properly.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|17|<p>Recommended settings: </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|18|<li> A value exceeding 100 for more than 15 minutes should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|19|<li> A value exceeding 500 for more than 30 minutes should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|20|<p><i>Average Latency</i> - The average time, in seconds, to receive, process and deliver the last 30 messages.  The value should normally be below 50 seconds.  If the latency consistently exceeds 50 seconds for more than 30 minutes <b><i>may</i></b>  indicate a problem that needs attention. Sometimes the value will rise temporarily and then go back down after 10 or 15 minutes. This is normal behavior.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|21|<p>Recommended settings: </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|22|<li> A value exceeding 50 seconds for more than 15 minutes should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|23|<li> A value exceeding 150 seconds for more than 30 minutes should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|24|<p><i>Last Message</i> - The time, in minutes, since the last message was received. For a busy machine, this value should normally be less than 5 minutes. A value consistently exceeding 20 minutes for more than 30 minutes <b><i>may</i></b>  indicate a problem that needs attention. Sometimes the value will rise temporarily and then go back down after 2 or 3 minutes.  This is normal behavior.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|25|<p>Recommended settings: </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|26|<li> A value exceeding 15 minutes should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|27|<li> A value exceeding 30 minutes should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|28|<p><i>CPU 1/CPU 2 Fan Speed</i> - Should be between 3,000 and 5,000 (RPM)</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|29|<p>Recommended settings:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|30|<li> A value for either CPU fan that falls below 2500 should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|31|<li> A value for either CPU fan that falls below 500 should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|32|<p><i>Firmware Storage</i> - Typical value (in percent) is 60 - 80%. A value above 80% usually means that a debug file needs to be deleted.  This can be done on a non-emergency basis.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|33|<p>Recommended settings:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|34|<li> A value above 80% should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|35|<li> A value above 90% should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|36|<p><i>Mail/Log Storage</i> -  - Typical value (in percent) is 1 - 70%.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|37|<p>Recommended settings:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|38|<li> A value above 70% should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|39|<li> A value above 80% should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|40|<p><i>System Load</i> - The system's load (in percent.) During normal operation, this value can vary wildly, anywhere between 1 and 100%.  A value that remains at 100% for more than 2 hours <b><i>may</i></b>  indicate a problem that needs attention. The value may rise temporarily, then go back down after 2 or 3 minutes. This is normal behavior.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|41|<p>Recommended settings:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|42|<li> A value above 80% for more than 1 hour should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|43|<li> A value above 90% for more than 3 hours should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|44|<p><i>CPU Temperature</i> - Should be between 40 and 70 degrees C</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|45|<p>Recommended settings:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|46|<li> A value above 70 degrees C for more than 30 minutes should result in a <b>Warning</b>. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Barracuda/Barracuda HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.barracuda.http.txt|47|<li> A value above 80 degrees C for more than 1 hour should result in an <b>Alarm</b>.</li>

Servers-Standard/Basic TCP|com.dartware.tcp.basic|05|<p>This basic TCP probe tests whether a TCP port accepts connections. If the specified port fails to accept the TCP connection within sixty seconds, the device state is set to <b>Down</b>.</p>

Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|03|<h3>Basic TCP (Blocked)</h3>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|05|<p>This basic TCP probe tests that a TCP port is <b>not</b> accepting connections. This probe may be used to test that a firewall is working properly, or that a particular TCP service is never operating on an important machine.</p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|06|<p>If the specified port accepts the TCP connection, the device state is set to the selected state. Otherwise, the device status is set to <b>OKAY</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|08|<p><i>Failure Status</i> - The device status upon successful connection. The default state is <b><i>DOWN</i></b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Basic TCP (Blocked)|com.dartware.tcp.blocked|09|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.blocked</span><br />

Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|01|<h2>Servers Proprietary &gt; Citrix Server<a name="Servers_Proprietary_Citrix_Server"></a></h2>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|03|<h3>Citrix Server</h3>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|05|<p>This probe connects to a Citrix server, using default port 1494. It checks for the presence of the string "ICA" in the response, which indicates that the Citrix server is running.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|06|<p>This probe sets the device to <b>Alarm</b> if:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|07|<li> a disconnect is received unexpectedly. </li>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|08|<li> doesn't receive a response within 30 seconds after connecting</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|09|<li> the response doesn't contain the string "ICA"</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|10|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Citrix Server|com.dartware.tcp.citrix.txt|11|<p>None.</p>

Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Custom TCP<a name="Servers_Standard_Custom_TCP"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|03|<h3>Custom TCP</h3>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|05|<p>This probe sends the specified string over a TCP connection, and sets the status of the device based on the response. Six parameters control the operation of this probe:</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|07|<p><i>String to send</i> - The initial string sent to the device via TCP. This could be a command which indicates what to test, or a combination of a command and a password. The string is sent on its own line, terminated by a CR-LF.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|08|<p><i>Seconds to wait</i> - The number of seconds to wait for a response.  If no response is received within the specified number of seconds, the device's status is set to <b>Down</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|09|<p><i>OK Response</i> - The substring to match the device's "ok response". If it matches the first line received, the device is reported to have a status of OK.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|10|<p><i>WARN Response</i> - The substring to match the device's <b>Warning</b> response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|11|<p><i>ALRM Response</i> - The substring to match the device's <b>Alarm</b> response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|12|<p><i>CRIT Response</i> - The substring to match the device's <b>Critical</b> response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|13|<p><i>DOWN Response</i> - The substring to match the device's <b>Down</b> response.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|14|<p>If InterMapper cannot connect to the specified TCP port, the device's status is set to <b>Down</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|15|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.custom</span><br />
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|16|Version:  <span class="code">1.10</span></p>
Servers-Standard/Custom TCP|com.dartware.tcp.custom|17|<p><a href="Servers_Standard.htm">Back to Top</a></p>

Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; CVS Server<a name="Servers_Standard_CVS_Server"></a></h2>

Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|03|<h3>CVS Server</h3>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|05|<p>This probe tests a CVS server by connecting to the specified port and authentication strings as shown below. By default, the port is 2401.</p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|06|<p><span class="code">BEGIN AUTH REQUEST&lt;lf&gt;</span></p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|07|<p>CVSROOT_Path&lt;lf&gt;</p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|08|<p>Username&lt;lf&gt;</p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|09|<p>Scrambled_password&lt;lf&gt;</p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|10|<p>END AUTH REQUEST&lt;lf&gt;</p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|11|<p>If the response is "I LOVE YOU", then the authentication succeeded.</p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|12|<p>If the response is "I HATE YOU", then either the authentication failed or the path to CVSROOT is incorrect.</p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|13|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|14|<p><i>CVSROOT_path</i> - Path to the CVS server</p>

Servers-Standard/CVS Server|com.dartware.tcp.cvs|16|<p><i>Password</i> - User's password</p>

Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|03|<h3>FTP (Login)</h3>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|05|<p>The standard protocol for transferring files on TCP/IP internets, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc0959.txt">RFC 959</a>.  The default TCP port number for FTP control connections is port 21.</p>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|06|<p>This TCP probe connects to the FTP server's control port (21). It then logs in using the specified User ID and Password and issues a NOOP command. If the connection is successful, the probe issues the QUIT command and sets the status to <b>Okay</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|08|<p><i>User ID</i> - the account name used to login to the FTP server.</p>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|09|<p><i>Password</i> - the account password used to verify the User ID's identity.</p>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|10|<p><b>Note:</b>  If the probe queries the FTP server often, and at regular intervals, the FTP server's log files contain a succession of "Login" and "Logout" log lines.</p>
Servers-Standard/FTP/FTP (Login)|com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.ftp.login</span><br />

Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; HTTP &amp; HTTPS &gt; HTTP<a name="Servers_Standard_HTTP___HTTPS_HTTP"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|03|<h3>HTTP</h3>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|05|<p>The protocol used to transfer web pages on the World Wide Web, defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2068.txt">RFC 2068</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1945.txt">RFC 1945</a>. The default TCP port number for HTTP connections is port 80.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|06|<p>This TCP probe lets you download a specific web page and scan it for a specific string of HTML.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|08|<p><i>Host Name</i> - the domain name of the web server (e.g. "www.intermapper.com"). This can be derived from the host name part of the URL that you want to test. You must enter a valid "Host Name" to test web servers which implement virtual hosts. Only add an IP address or domain name; do not add "http://".</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|09|<p><i>URL Path</i> - - the full path of the desired file on the web server (e.g. "/index.html"). The first character must be a '/'.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|10|<p><i>String to verify</i> - the string to verify in the data returned by the HTTP server.  For example, if you are retrieving a web page, you might search for "&lt;HTML" or "&lt;P&gt;" to verify that the data is HTML. If this string is not found, the device will go into alarm.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|11|<p><i>User ID</i> - the user name typed into the web browser's password dialog. The default is to leave this blank. You should set this parameter if you want to test a web page that requires authentication.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|12|<p><i>Password</i> - the password for the web browser's dialog. The default is to leave this blank. You should set this parameter if you want to test a web page that requires authentication.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|13|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.http</span><br />
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|14|Version:  <span class="code">2.12</span></p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|15|<p><a href="Servers_Standard.htm">Back to Top</a></p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP|com.dartware.tcp.http|16|</blockquote>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|00|<li><a href="Servers_Standard.htm#Servers_Standard_HTTP___HTTPS_HTTP__Post_">Servers Standard &gt; HTTP &amp; HTTPS &gt; HTTP (Post)<MadCap:xref href="Servers_Standard.htm#Servers_Standard_HTTP___HTTPS_HTTP__Post_" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; HTTP &amp; HTTPS &gt; HTTP (Post)<a name="Servers_Standard_HTTP___HTTPS_HTTP__Post_"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|03|<h3>HTTP (Post)</h3>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|05|<p>  The protocol used to transfer web pages on the World Wide Web, defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2068.txt">RFC 2068</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1945.txt">RFC 1945</a>.  The default TCP port number for HTTP connections is port 80.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|06|<p>  This TCP probe lets you post form results to a specific web CGI.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|08|<p>  <i>Host Name</i> - the domain name of the web server (e.g. "www.intermapper.com"). This can be derived from the host name part of the URL that you want to test.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|09|<p>  <i>URL Path</i> - the full path to the desired CGI on the web server (e.g. "/index.cgi"). The first character must be a '/'.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|10|<p>  <i>Form Data</i> - the encoded data sent in the body of the POST message.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Post)|com.dartware.tcp.http.cgi.post|11|<p>  <i>String to verify</i> - a string expected to find in HTTP server's response. For example, if you post form data that is designed to generate an error, you might search for "sorry" or "could not be processed" to verify that the CGI is properly rejecting the data. If this string is not found, the device will go into alarm.</p>

Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; HTTP &amp; HTTPS &gt; HTTP (Follow Redirects)<a name="Servers_Standard_HTTP___HTTPS_HTTP__Follow_Redirects_"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|03|<h3>HTTP (Follow Redirects)</h3>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|05|<p>The protocol used to transfer web pages on the World Wide Web, defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2068.txt">RFC 2068</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1945.txt">RFC 1945</a>. The default TCP port number for HTTP connections is port 80.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|06|<p>This TCP probe lets you download a specific web page and scan it for a specific string of HTML. This probe will follow a limitd number of page redirects to the same HTTP server.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|08|<p><i>Host Name</i> - the domain name of the web server (Example: "www.intermapper.com"). This can be derived from the host name part of the URL that you want to test. You must enter a valid <i>Host Name</i> to test a web server that implements a virtual host. Add only an IP address or domain name; do not add "http://".</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|09|<p><i>URL Path</i> - the full path of the desired file on the web server (Example: "/index.html"). The first character must be a '/'.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|10|<p><i>String to verify</i> - a string to verify in the server's response. For example, if you are retrieving a web page, you could search for "&lt;HTML" or "&lt;P&gt;" to verify that the data is HTML. If the string is not found, the device goes into <b>Alarm</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|11|<p><i>User ID</i> - the user name typed into the web browser's password dialog. Leave this blank unless you want to test a web page that requires authentication.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|12|<p><i>Password</i> - the password for the web browser's dialog. Leave this blank unless you want to test a web page that requires authentication.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|13|<p><i>Redirect Limit</i> is the maximum number of redirects to follow.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Follow Redirects)|com.dartware.tcp.http.follow|14|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.http.follow</span><br />

Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|03|<h3>HTTP (Proxy)</h3>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|05|<p>The protocol used to transfer web pages on the World Wide Web, defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2068.txt">RFC 2068</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1945.txt">RFC 1945</a>. The default TCP port number for HTTP connections is port 80.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|06|<p>This TCP probe lets you test that a web server can be accessed using a remote proxy server as an intermediary. For example, this probe can check if your web server is accessible from some remote location on the Internet (e.g. www.proxymate.com).</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|08|<p><i>URL</i> is the full URL to the desired page on the web server,including the "http://" scheme (e.g. "http://www.intermapper.com")</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|09|<p><i>Proxy User ID</i> is your user ID for the proxy server. Leave this field blank if no authentication is required to use the proxy server.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|10|<p><i>Proxy Password</i> is your password for the proxy server. Leave this field blank if no authentication is required to use the proxy server.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|11|<p><i>String to verify</i> is a string to verify in the data returned by the HTTP server.  For example, if you are retrieving a web page, you might search for "&lt;HTML" or "&lt;P&gt;" to verify that the data is HTML. If this string is not found, the device will go into alarm.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTP (Proxy)|com.dartware.tcp.http.proxy|12|<p><i>User Agent</i> is the string that identifies this InterMapper client probe to the proxy web server. Some proxy servers block traffic at the proxy based on the User-Agent identity. This parameter lets you optionally override InterMapper's default User-Agent setting. If you leave this parameter blank, InterMapper sends a User-Agent  string of "InterMapper/version", where version is the current version number of InterMapper.</p>

Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTPS (Redirect)|com.dartware.tcp.https.redirect.txt|05|<p>The protocol used to transfer web pages on the World Wide Web, defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2068.txt">RFC 2068</a> and  <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1945.txt">RFC 1945</a>. Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTPS (Redirect)|com.dartware.tcp.https.redirect.txt|09|<p><i>URL Path</i> - the full path of the desired file on the web server (Example: "/index.html"). The first character must be a '/'.</p>

Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTPS (Redirect)|com.dartware.tcp.https.redirect.txt|11|<p><i>User ID</i> - the user name typed into the web browser's password dialog. The default is to leave this blank. You should set this parameter if you want to test a web page that requires authentication.</p>
Servers-Standard/HTTP & HTTPS/HTTPS (Redirect)|com.dartware.tcp.https.redirect.txt|12|<p><i>Password</i> - the password for the web browser's dialog. Leave this blank unless you want to test a web page that requires authentication.</p>

Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|00|<li><a href="Experimental.htm#Experimental_InterMapper">Experimental &gt; InterMapper<MadCap:xref href="Experimental.htm#Experimental_InterMapper" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|01|<h2>Experimental &gt; InterMapper<a name="Experimental_InterMapper"></a></h2>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|02|<blockquote>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|03|<h3>InterMapper</h3>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|05|<p>This probe monitors the status of the InterMapper polling engine. With the default setting, this probe displays the results of 500 loops through the polling engine. To measure activity at a finer-grain, decrease the value of the <i>Loops</i> parameter. A value of '1' updates the statistics on every pass through the main run loop.</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|06|<p>The "Main Loop" frequency is the number of times that InterMapper performs the main loop each second. The theoretical maximum loop frequency is 66.667 loops per second, based on the current yield value of 15 msec. If it falls below 10 or even 5 loops per second, InterMapper may report false outages.</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|07|<p>This probe also reports polling rate as a percentage of the maximum loops per second. This is a measure of how much additional processing occurs per loop. This percentage will never be 100%. It should, however, level out and remain steady over time.</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|08|<p>On Unix systems, this probe reports Context Switches Per Loop (CSPL). This is another measure of the overhead of InterMapper's processing as it runs on your system. Fewer context switches per loop is better (ideal = 0), since context switches carry overhead. A server with thousands of devices and hundreds of mays may well have a CSPL greater than 2 during normal operation. (This value is not available on Windows systems, and is alway set to -1.)</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|09|<p>InterMapper tracks the number of bytes sent out the main UDP polling socket. Bytes/Loop is the average bytes sent per loop, averaged over the last batch of N loops. Bytes Peak is the maximum number of bytes sent in a *single* polling loop.  (In the current implementation, the peak bytes is checked on every loop, but only resets to 0 when you change the # loops parameter; ie peak bytes is not the peak bytes of the last batch of N loops.)</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|10|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|11|<p><i>Loops</i> - the number of loops to perform before updating statistics.</p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|12|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt</span><br />
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|13|Version:  <span class="code">0.9</span></p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|14|<p><a href="Experimental.htm">Back to Top</a></p>
Experimental/InterMapper|com.dartware.tcp.intermapper.txt|15|</blockquote>

Servers-Standard/IRC|com.dartware.tcp.irc|09|<p><i>Username</i> - the username, hostname, servername and realname of the new user. Typically, the hostname and servername are ignored for client connections. The realname must be prefixed with a ':'.</p>
Servers-Standard/IRC|com.dartware.tcp.irc|10|<p><i>String to verify</i> - a string to verify in the IRC server's response. For example, you might check for a string returned in the IRC server's welcome message.</p>

Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|03|<h3>LDAP</h3>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|05|<p>The protocol used to access directories supporting the X.500 models, as described in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2251.txt">RFC 2251</a>.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|06|<p>This probe connects to the LDAP server and binds using the designated <i>Bind Name</i>. If a <i>Bind Password</i> is provided, it is sent as clear text to authenticate the probe.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|07|<p>Once logged in, the probe sends a SearchRequest for <i>Field to Match</i> searching for an equality match of <i>Name to Lookup</i>, and counts the number of LDAP records returned.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|08|<p>If the <i>Search Base</i> field is specified, this value is used as the base of the search. Otherwise, the <i>Bind Name</i> is used for the Base DN.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|09|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|10|<p><i>Bind Name</i> and <i>Bind Password</i> - used to connect to the LDAP server.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|11|<p><i>Name to Lookup</i> - string to use in the SearchRequest.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|12|<p><i>Search Base</i> - optional base for the search.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|13|<p><i>Field to Match[cn,sn,uid]</i> - enter one of the listed fields to check for a match.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|14|<p><i>Minimum No. of Results</i> - enter an expected minimum number of records returned.</p>
Servers-Standard/LDAP/LDAP|com.dartware.tcp.ldap|15|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.ldap</span><br />
