Servers-Standard/NNTP|com.dartware.tcp.nntp|03|<h3>NNTP</h3>
Servers-Standard/NNTP|com.dartware.tcp.nntp|05|<p>The protocol used to read network news on TCP/IP Internets, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc0977.txt">RFC 977</a>.  The default TCP port number for NNTP connections is port 119.</p>
Servers-Standard/NNTP|com.dartware.tcp.nntp|06|<p>This script connects to a news server and uses the GROUP command to request information about a specific newsgroup name. The script then issues the QUIT command to tell the server it is closing the connection.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|00|<li><a href="Servers_Proprietary.htm#Servers_Proprietary_Nagios_NRPE">Servers Proprietary &gt; Nagios NRPE<MadCap:xref href="Servers_Proprietary.htm#Servers_Proprietary_Nagios_NRPE" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|01|<h2>Servers Proprietary &gt; Nagios NRPE<a name="Servers_Proprietary_Nagios_NRPE"></a></h2>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|03|<h3>Nagios NRPE</h3>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|05|<p>The NRPE ("Nagios Remote Plugin Executor") protocol defines a way to execute Nagios plugins on remote machines. After you install a Nagios NRPE daemon and and one or more Nagios plugins on a remote machine, InterMapper uses the following procedure to retrieve the status of that machine.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|06|<li> Establish an encrypted SSL/TLS connection to the remote NRPE daemon</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|07|<li> Request that a specific Nagios plugin be executed</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|08|<li> Receive the response from the plugin</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|09|<li> Parse the response and display the state of that machine.</li>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|10|<p>The NRPE daemon uses a configuration file (<i>nrpe.cfg</i>) that has command definition entries in this form:</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|11|<p><span class="code">  command[check_swap]=/usr/local/nagios/libexec/check_swap -w 20% -c 10%</span></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|12|<p>When the NRPE daemon receives a request to run the "check_swap" plugin, it issues the command above.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|13|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|14|<p><i>Nagios Plugin</i> - tells which plugin to execute. It must match one of the command definitions in the nrpe.cfg file (the text within square brackets [ ... ]). To test the connection from InterMapper to the NRPE daemon, set <i>Nagios Plugin</i> to the value "_NRPE_CHECK".</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|15|<p>For information about installing an NRPE daemon, see the <a href="http://nagios.sourceforge.net/docs/nrpe/NRPE.pdf">NRPE Documentation</a> (at http://nagios.sourceforge.net/docs/nrpe/NRPE.pdf), especially the section on Remote Host Configuration. Nagios and the Nagios logo are registered trademarks of Ethan Galstad. For more information, see <a href="http://www.nagios.org.">http://www.nagios.org.</a> </p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|16|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt</span><br />
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|17|Version:  <span class="code">1.2</span></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|18|<p><a href="Servers_Proprietary.htm">Back to Top</a></p>
Servers-Proprietary/Nagios NRPE|com.dartware.tcp.nrpe.txt|19|</blockquote>

Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Mail &gt; POP3<a name="Servers_Standard_Mail_POP3"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|03|<h3>POP3</h3>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|05|<p>The protocol used to access email messages from a central maildrop server, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1939.txt">RFC 1939</a>.  The default TCP port number for POP3 connections is port 110.</p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|07|<p><i>User Name</i> - if left empty, the probe verifies that the server sends "+OK" as its initial greeting, then immediately sends the QUIT command. If specified, the probe attempts to use the specified <i>Password</i> to login to the POP3 server. If the login fails , the device is set to <b>Warning</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|08|<p><i>Use APOP if supported</i> - By default, the probe uses the APOP command to authenticate the user if the server supports it. To authenticate via USER and PASS commands for a particular user, set this parameter to <b><i>False</i></b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|09|<p><b>Note:</b> If APOP is not supported by the server, the <i>Use APOP if supported</i> option has no effect.</p>
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|10|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.pop3</span><br />
Servers-Standard/Mail/POP3|com.dartware.tcp.pop3|11|Version:  <span class="code">2.7</span></p>

Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Multimedia &gt; RTSP<a name="Servers_Standard_Multimedia_RTSP"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|03|<h3>RTSP</h3>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|05|<p>The protocol used to control real-time streams, defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc2326.txt">RFC 2326</a> and <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1889.txt">RFC 1889</a>.  The default TCP port number for RTSP connections is port 554.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|06|<p>This TCP probe lets you check that the server is up and responding.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|07|<p>The specifics of the commands that the probe must send to the server vary somewhat depending upon the version of RFC2326 that the server implements:</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|08|<li> If the server you're monitoring implements RFC2326bis-02 or later, then set <b>RFC2326bis-02 or later</b> to "Yes". </li>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|09|<li> *If you're not sure, leave it set to "No". </li>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|10|<li> *If the device goes into <b><i>Warning</i></b> with the reason set to "[RTSP] Unexpected response to PLAY command. (RTSP/1.0 460 Only Aggregate Option Allowed)", then set it to "Yes".</li>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|11|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|12|<p><i>Movie Name</i> - the name of the file you want to stream.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|13|<p><i>Seconds to play</i> - the number of seconds you want to stream the specified file.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|14|<p><i>RFC2326bis-02 or later</i> - indicate whether the RFC2326 version is RFC2326bis-02 or newer.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/RTSP|com.dartware.tcp.rtsp|15|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.rtsp</span><br />

Servers-Standard/SNPP|com.dartware.tcp.snpp|03|<h3>SNPP</h3>
Servers-Standard/SNPP|com.dartware.tcp.snpp|05|<p>This protocol transfers pager information across the Internet, as defined in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc1861.txt">RFC 1861</a>.  The default TCP port number for SMTP connections is port 444.</p>
Servers-Standard/SNPP|com.dartware.tcp.snpp|06|<p>This SNPP probe verifies that an SNPP server is working by connecting to it and issuing a PAGE &lt;pagerid&gt; command. If it receives a valid response code, the probe issues a QUIT command and exits, setting device status to <b>OK</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/SNPP|com.dartware.tcp.snpp|07|<p>If an "Invalid Pager ID" response is received, the probe issues a QUIT command and exits, setting device status to <b>Alarm</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/SNPP|com.dartware.tcp.snpp|08|<p>If no connection was made, or if an unexpected response is received, device status is set to <b>Down</b>.</p>
Servers-Standard/SNPP|com.dartware.tcp.snpp|09|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/SNPP|com.dartware.tcp.snpp|10|<p><i>PagerID</i> - your Pager ID on the specified SNPP server.</p>

Servers-Standard/Subversion/SVN (Apache)|com.dartware.tcp.svn.apache|03|<h3>SVN (Apache)</h3>
Servers-Standard/Subversion/SVN (Apache)|com.dartware.tcp.svn.apache|05|<p>This probe tests a Subversion server running as an Apache module. The subversion module lets Apache function as a WebDAV/DeltaV server. Since the server responds normally to HTTP GET requests, testing whether it is up is the same as performing an HTTP GET request and checking to ensure the location was found.</p>
Servers-Standard/Subversion/SVN (Apache)|com.dartware.tcp.svn.apache|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>

Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Telnet<a name="Servers_Standard_Telnet"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|03|<h3>Telnet</h3>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|05|<p>The protocol used for terminal-to-terminal communication and distributed computation as described in <a href="http://www.ietf.org/rfc/rfc0854.txt">RFC 854</a>. The default TCP port number for Telnet connections is port 23.</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|06|<p>This probe lets you Telnet to a device, login with a name and password, and optionally enter a command. The probe is specifically designed to reject any Telnet options proffered by the Telnet server; the TCP connection always remains in the base "network virtual terminal" state. You can enter data at up to three prompts.</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|08|<p><i>Intro String to Match</i> - a string to match in the welcome banner sent by the Telnet server when you first connect. Leave this parameter blank to match anything in the welcome banner.</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|09|<p><i>First Prompt</i> - the string to match in the first prompt. (example: "Login:")</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|10|<p><i>Reply #1</i> - your reply to the first prompt. (example: your response to the "Login:" prompt)</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|11|<p><i>Second Prompt</i> - the string to match in the second prompt. (example: "Password:") If this parameter is empty, the probe ignores the prompt string and it does not send a reply.</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|12|<p><i>Reply #2</i> - your reply to the second prompt, such as your response to the "Password:" prompt.</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|13|<p><i>Third Prompt</i> - the string to match in the third prompt. If this parameter is empty, the probe ignores the prompt string and its reply.</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|14|<p><i>Reply #3</i> - your reply to the third prompt.</p>
Servers-Standard/Telnet|com.dartware.tcp.telnet|15|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.tcp.telnet</span><br />

Servers-Standard/VNC Server|com.dartware.tcp.vnc|05|<p>Attempt to connect to a VNC Server. VNC uses RFB (Remote Frame Buffer) protocol for communication between clients and server.  The probe waits to receive a "RFB ###.###" string. If it arrives, the VNC server is assumed to be up and the probe simply disconnects.</p>
Servers-Standard/VNC Server|com.dartware.tcp.vnc|06|<p>The Virtual Network Computer (VNC) protocol was originally designed at AT&amp;T Labs in Cambridge. Servers-Proprietary/Apple/Xserve/Xserve G4|com.dartware.tcp.xserve.details|06|<p><b>Note:</b> It is compatible Xserve G4s running Mac OS X 10.3.9 and earlier.  For Xserves running 10.4 or later, please choose the Xserve Tiger probe.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Apple/Xserve/Xserve G4|com.dartware.tcp.xserve.details|09|<p><i>User</i> - the name of any user on the specified server.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Apple/Xserve/Xserve G4|com.dartware.tcp.xserve.details|14|<p><i>Drives</i> - information about the drives installed on the server. Includes the manufacturer, model, and capacity of each drive.</p>

Servers-Proprietary/Apple/Xserve/Xserve G4|com.dartware.tcp.xserve.details|17|<p><i>Temperature</i> - the ambient temperature of the server.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apple/Xserve/Xserve G4|com.dartware.tcp.xserve.details|18|<p><i>Blowers</i> - information on the speed of the server's cooling fans.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apple/Xserve/Xserve G4|com.dartware.tcp.xserve.details|19|<p><i>Security</i> - the state of the security lock and the enclosure.</p>
Servers-Proprietary/Apple/Xserve/Xserve G4|com.dartware.tcp.xserve.details|20|<p><b>Note:</b> The implementation of this probe uses OpenSSL on MacOSX.</p>

Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|01|<h2>Servers Standard &gt; Multimedia &gt; Multicast Listener<a name="Servers_Standard_Multimedia_Multicast_Listener"></a></h2>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|02|<blockquote>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|03|<h3>Multicast Listener</h3>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|05|<p>This probe listens for UDP packets directed to a specific UDP port. If you specify a multicast IP address, InterMapper listens for packets directed to that multicast address. If a packet isn't received within the specified number of seconds, the device status is set <b>DOWN</b>. The default is 10 seconds.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|06|<p>Use this probe to verify that a multicast source is broadcasting, for example, a live QuickTime broadcaster.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|07|<p>The probe does not inject any traffic into the network; it is passive only.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|08|<p><i>Multicast IP Address</i> - the optional multicast IP address to listen on.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|09|<p><i>Seconds to wait</i> - the maximum number of seconds to wait between packets.  If a packet is not received within the specified number of seconds, the device's status is set to DOWN. The timer is reset each time a packet is received.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|10|<p><i>Verify Source Address</i> - specify whether the probe should count packets only from the IP address of the targeted device.</p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.udplistener</span><br />
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|12|Version:  <span class="code">2.1</span></p>
Servers-Standard/Multimedia/Multicast Listener|com.dartware.udplistener|13|<p><a href="Servers_Standard.htm">Back to Top</a></p>

WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|00|<li><a href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_CPU_Utilization">WMI &gt; WMI CPU Utilization<MadCap:xref href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_CPU_Utilization" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|01|<h2>WMI &gt; WMI CPU Utilization<a name="WMI_WMI_CPU_Utilization"></a></h2>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|02|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|03|<h3>WMI CPU Utilization</h3>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to retrieve the percentage of time that a processor uses to execute a non-idle thread on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the PercentProcessorTime property of the Win32_PerfFormattedData_PerfOS_Processor class and compares it against the Warning and Critical parameters you set.  </p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|06|<p>The target host must be running Windows XP, Windows Server 2003 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|07|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|08|<p><i>Single Warning</i>, <i>Single Critical</i>, <i>Total Warning</i>, and <i>Total Critical</i> - the device's condition is set by comparing each processor against the specified Single percentages, and the total CPU utilization against the specified Total percentages. You can leave any of these values blank.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|09|<p><i>User</i> - may be a local user on the target host, or can take the form <span class="code">domain&#92;user</span> for a domain login. If authentication is not required (such as when the target is localhost,) leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|10|<p><i>Timeout (sec)</i> - the number of seconds to wait before assuming the host is not available.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|11|<p>InterMapper invokes the <span class="code">cpu_util.vbs</span> companion script, included with the probe. It uses the script's exit value to set the condition of the device. It uses the performance data returned by the script to create a nice display of chartable data.</p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|12|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt</span><br />
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|13|Version:  <span class="code">1.11</span></p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|14|<p><a href="WMI.htm">Back to Top</a></p>
WMI/WMI CPU Utilization|com.dartware.wmi.cpu_utilization.txt|15|</blockquote>

WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|01|<h2>WMI &gt; WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis<a name="WMI_WMI_Disk_Fragmentation_Analysis"></a></h2>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|02|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|03|<h3>WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis</h3>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to analyze disk fragmentation on a drive on the target host.  Specifically, it calls the DefragAnalysis method of the Win32_Volume class and reports pertinent statistics from the anaylsis.  If the drive needs to be defragmented, the device is set to <b>Warning</b>.  The target host must be running Windows Vista, Windows Server 2003 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|07|<p><i>Drive</i> - the drive letter assigned to the local disk to be analyzed, including the colon but without backslashes.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|08|<p><i>User</i> - may be a local user on the target host, or can take the form <span class="code">domain&#92;user</span> for a domain login. If authentication is not required (such as when the target is localhost,) leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|09|<p><i>Timeout (sec)</i> - the number of seconds to wait before assuming the host is not available.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|10|<p>InterMapper invokes the <span class="code">defrag_analysis.vbs</span> companion script, included with the probe. It uses the script's exit value to set the condition of the device. It uses the performance data returned by the script to create a nice display of chartable data.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Fragmentation Analysis|com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wmi.defrag_analysis.txt</span><br />

WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|00|<li><a href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_Disk_Available">WMI &gt; WMI Disk Available<MadCap:xref href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_Disk_Available" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|01|<h2>WMI &gt; WMI Disk Available<a name="WMI_WMI_Disk_Available"></a></h2>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|02|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|03|<h3>WMI Disk Available</h3>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to determine the disk space available on the specified drive(s) on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the Size and FreeSpace properties of the Win32_LogicalDisk class, computes percentage free space, and compares it against the specified values.  The target host must be running Windows 2000 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|07|<p><i>Drive</i> - May be set to "All" to check disk space on all of the host machine's local hard drives. Enter a list of comma-separated drive names (including the colon). These drives will be listed regardless of whether they are local hard drives. Zero-sized drives, such as an empty cd-rom, are not listed. The first drive with space that is less than the specified values is cited in the reason.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|08|<p><i>User</i> - may be a local user on the target host, or can take the form <span class="code">domain&#92;user</span> for a domain login. If authentication is not required (such as when the target is localhost,) leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|09|<p>InterMapper invokes the <span class="code">disk_avail.vbs</span> companion script included with the probe. It uses the script's exit value to set the condition of the device. It uses the performance data returned by the script to create a nice display of chartable data.</p>
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|10|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt</span><br />
WMI/WMI Disk Available|com.dartware.wmi.disk_available.txt|11|Version:  <span class="code">1.10</span></p>

WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|00|<li><a href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_Event_Log">WMI &gt; WMI Event Log<MadCap:xref href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_Event_Log" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|01|<h2>WMI &gt; WMI Event Log<a name="WMI_WMI_Event_Log"></a></h2>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|02|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|03|<h3>WMI Event Log</h3>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to retrieve entries from the Event Logs on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the Win32_NTLogEvent class, limiting the search with the parameters you set.  If matching events are found, a critical status is returned.  The target host must be running Windows 2000 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|07|<p><i>Log File</i> - contains a comma-separated list of the logs to be searched.  At least one Log File is required.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|08|<p><i>Event Codes</i> - a comma-separated list of event codes to search. To select all codes, leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|09|<p><i>Event Types</i> - a comma-separated list; can include event type names or corresponding numerical values.  Names and values can be intermixed. Limits the selection to events of the specified types.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|10|<p><i>Hours</i>, <i>Minutes</i>, and <i>Seconds</i> - combine to define how far back in the event log to search. The specified values are subtracted from the current time and used to select events, based on when they were written to the log.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|11|<p><i>User</i> - may be a local user on the target host, or can take the form <span class="code">domain&#92;user</span> for a domain login. If authentication is not required (such as when the target is localhost,) leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|12|<p><i>Timeout (sec)</i> - the number of seconds to wait before assuming the host is not available.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|13|<p>InterMapper invokes the <span class="code">event_log.vbs</span> companion script included with this probe.</p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|14|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt</span><br />
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|15|Version:  <span class="code">1.12</span></p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|16|<p><a href="WMI.htm">Back to Top</a></p>
WMI/WMI Event Log|com.dartware.wmi.event_log.txt|17|</blockquote>

WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|01|<h2>WMI &gt; WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server<a name="WMI_WMI_MSExchange_2007_Mailbox_Server"></a></h2>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|02|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|03|<h3>WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server</h3>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to retrieve performance information about the delivery queues on a MS Exchange 2007 Mailbox Server.  Specifically, it queries the Win32_PerfFormattedData_MSExchangeIS_MSExchangeIS, Win32_PerfFormattedData_MSExchangeIS_MSExchangeISMailbox, Win32_PerfFormattedData_MSExchangeIS_MSExchangeISPublic, Win32_PerfFormattedData_MSExchangeSearchIndices_MSExchangeSearchIndices classes to collect a variety of statistics and then compares them to the criteria you set.  The default criteria for warning and critical conditions are taken from the Microsoft TechNet article <a href="http://technet.microsoft.com/en-us/library/bb201689.aspx">Monitoring Mailbox Servers</a>.</p>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|07|<p><i>User</i> - may be a local user on the target host, or can take the form <span class="code">domain&#92;user</span> for a domain login. If authentication is not required (such as when the target is localhost,) leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|08|<p><i>Timeout (sec)</i> - the number of seconds to wait before assuming the host is not available.</p>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|09|<p>InterMapper invokes the <span class="code">ex07_mailbox.vbs</span> companion script included with this probe. It uses the script's exit value to set the condition of the device.</p>
WMI/WMI MSExchange 2007 Mailbox Server|com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt|10|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wmi.ex07_mailbox_server.txt</span><br />

WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|01|<h2>WMI &gt; WMI File Check<a name="WMI_WMI_File_Check"></a></h2>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|02|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|03|<h3>WMI File Check</h3>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to retrieve information about files on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the CIM_DataFile class, limiting the search with the parameters you set.  The target host must be running Windows 2000 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|07|<p><i>Path</i> - the location of the files to be checked. Include the drive, and enclose the path in double-quotes if it contains spaces.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|08|<p><i>File</i> - the filename and extension of the file you wish to check. The path is prepended to filename during the final query. To check all files that met the specified Size or time criteria, leave this parameter blank. You may also use a list of comma-separated filenames.  </p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|09|<p>Wildcards (* ?) may be used in the filename. When using wildcards, be sure to specify the Path parameter. Otherwise, the query could take an inordinate amount of time. At least one of <i>File</i> or <i>Path</i> must be set.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|10|<p><i>Size</i> - the minimum filesize in bytes. Any file larger than this value is listed. </p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|11|<p><i>Hours</i>, <i>Minutes</i> and <i>Seconds</i> - specify how recently the file was changed in order to be listed, based on the file's LastModified value. At least one of these parameters must be set.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|12|<p><i>User</i> - may be a local user on the target host, or can take the form <span class="code">domain&#92;user</span> for a domain login. If authentication is not required (such as when the target is localhost,) leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|13|<p><i>Timeout (sec)</i> - the number of seconds to wait before assuming the host is not available.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|14|<p>InterMapper invokes the <span class="code">file_chk.vbs</span> companion script, included with the probe. It lists the files which meet the specified criteria, and uses the exit value to set the condition of the device.</p>
WMI/WMI File Check|com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt|15|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wmi.file_check.txt</span><br />

WMI/WMI Folder Check|com.dartware.wmi.folder_check.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to retrieve information about a folder on the target host. It also notes the most recently modified file in the tree. The target host must be running Windows 2000 or later.</p>

It compares OutputQueueLength against the Warning and Critical parameters you set.  The target host must be running Windows XP, Windows Server 2003 or later.</p>

WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|00|<li><a href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_Top_Processes">WMI &gt; WMI Top Processes<MadCap:xref href="WMI.htm#WMI_WMI_Top_Processes" target="" title="" alt="" MadCap:conditions="Primary.print"></MadCap:xref></a></li>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|01|<h2>WMI &gt; WMI Top Processes<a name="WMI_WMI_Top_Processes"></a></h2>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|02|<blockquote>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|03|<h3>WMI Top Processes</h3>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|05|<p>This probe uses WMI to retrieve information about CPU utilization and processes running on the target host.  Specifically, it queries the PercentProcessorTime property of the Win32_PerfFormattedData_PerfOS_Processor class and compares it against the specified thresholds. It queries the PercentProcessorTime property of the Win32_PerfFormattedData_PerfProc_Process class and lists up to five processes using the most CPU time.  Because there is a time lapse between collecting the CPU data and the process data, the reported values do not add up exactly. The target host must be running Windows XP, Windows Server 2003 or later.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|07|<p><i>Warning</i> and <i>Critical</i> - set a value in percent to use as the threshold to set the device to this condition.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|08|<p><i>User</i> - may be a local user on the target host, or can take the form <span class="code">domain&#92;user</span> for a domain login. If authentication is not required (such as when the target is localhost,) leave this parameter blank.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|09|<p><i>Timeout (sec)</i> - the number of seconds to wait before assuming the host is not available.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|10|<p>InterMapper invokes the <span class="code">top_cpu.vbs</span> companion script, included with the probe. The probe uses script's the exit value to set the condition of the device. It also uses the performance data returned by the script to create a nice display of chartable data.</p>
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|11|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt</span><br />
WMI/WMI Top Processes|com.dartware.wmi.top_process.txt|12|Version:  <span class="code">1.11</span></p>

Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|01|<h2>Wireless &gt; smartBridges &gt; airPoint<a name="Wireless_smartBridges_airPoint"></a></h2>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|02|<blockquote>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|03|<h3>airPoint</h3>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|05|<p>This probe monitors a <a href="http://www.smartbridges.com">smartBridges</a> airPoint device. It retrieves and displays information from the AT76C510 MIB using SNMP v1. Depending on the bridge's operating mode this probe will display different information. </p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|06|<p>If device is operating as a wireless client or a wireless repeater, the probe will display information about the connection to the parent access point (ESSID, SSID, channel, RSSI, link quality). </p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|07|<p>If the device is operating as a wireless bridge (either point-to-point or point-to-multipoint), the probe will display the list of authorized MAC addresses. </p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|08|<p>If the operating mode is a wireless repeater or access point, the probe will monitor the number of clients and list each one with its RSSI/link quality. </p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|09|<p>It retrieves and displays a number of traffic (bytes received/transmitted) and physical variables (name, MAC address, firmware revision). </p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|10|<p>This probe may not return complete information to SNMPv1 clients using the community string "public". To fully utilize this probe, you must set the community string to the one with the correct permissions.</p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|11|<p><b>Note:</b> Install InterMapper on a machine where you don't plan to run smartBridges simpleMonitor. To run both InterMapper and smartBridges' simpleMonitor on the same machine, disable trap processing in InterMapper.</p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|12|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|13|<p><i>Number of clients warning</i>, <i>Maximum number of clients</i>, </p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|14|<p><i>Too many failed packets/sec</i>, <i>Too many retry packets/sec</i></p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|15|<li> enter thresholds for <b>Warning</b> and <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|16|<p><i>Link to Device Management Tool</i> - enter the URL to the web manager for this device. </p>
Wireless/smartBridges/airPoint|com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt|17|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wrls.airpoint.txt</span><br />

Wireless/Atmel/Atmel AT76C510|com.dartware.wrls.AT76C510.txt|01|<h2>Wireless &gt; Atmel &gt; Atmel AT76C510<a name="Wireless_Atmel_Atmel_AT76C510"></a></h2>
Wireless/Atmel/Atmel AT76C510|com.dartware.wrls.AT76C510.txt|02|<blockquote>
Wireless/Atmel/Atmel AT76C510|com.dartware.wrls.AT76C510.txt|03|<h3>Atmel AT76C510</h3>
Wireless/Atmel/Atmel AT76C510|com.dartware.wrls.AT76C510.txt|05|<p>This probe monitors devices based on the Atmel AT76C510 chip. Please refer to your device's technical specification to find out the chip type. Sample devices based on AT76C510 chip are as follows: Belkin F5D6130, D-Link DWL 900AP (rev. 1), Netgear ME102, and Linksys WAP11 (ver &lt; 2).</p>
Wireless/Atmel/Atmel AT76C510|com.dartware.wrls.AT76C510.txt|06|<p>It retrieves and displays information from the AT76C510 MIB using SNMP v1. Depending on the brige's operating mode this probe will display different information. </p>
Wireless/Atmel/Atmel AT76C510|com.dartware.wrls.AT76C510.txt|07|<p>If device is operating as a wireless client or a wireless repeater, the probe will display information about the connection to the parent access point (ESSID, SSID, channel, RSSI, link quality). </p>
Wireless/Atmel/Atmel AT76C510|com.dartware.wrls.AT76C510.txt|08|<p>If the device is operating as a wireless bridge (either point-to-point or point-to-multipoint), the probe will display the list of authorized MAC addresses. </p>

Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|01|<h2>Wireless &gt; MikroTik &gt; WDS Bridge<a name="Wireless_MikroTik_WDS_Bridge"></a></h2>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|02|<blockquote>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|03|<h3>WDS Bridge</h3>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|05|<p>This probe monitors a MikroTik router in WDS Bridge mode. The probe monitors the Ethernet traffic information, as well as device utilization (CPU, Disk, Memory loads). The probe also displays the signal strength and tx/rx rates of the wireless link.</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|06|<p>You must specify both the MAC address of the other AP, as well as the ifIndex of the wireless interface. The MAC address must be entered as six decimal numbers separated by "."</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|07|<p>To determine the ifIndex of the wireless interface, Telnet to the radio, then: </p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|08|<p>1) Log into the router</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|09|<p>2) Enter <span class="code">interface wireless print oid</span></p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|10|<p>3) The interface index is the last digit of the OIDs</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|11|<p>4) Type this number into the "Wireless Interface" field below.</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|12|<p>This probe will raise an alarm if the CPU, Disk, or Memory loads exceeds the High Use Threshold.</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|13|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|14|<p><i>Associated AP MAC Adrs</i> - the MAC address of Access Point to which the router is connected.</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|15|<p><i>Wireless Interface</i> - the index of the interface </p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|16|<p><i>High Use Threshold (%)</i> - the usage threshold to trigger <b>Alarm</b>.</p>
Wireless/MikroTik/WDS Bridge|com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt|17|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wrls.mikrotik-wds.txt</span><br />

Wireless/Tranzeo/Tranzeo (PXP)|com.dartware.wrls.tranzeopxp.txt|03|<h3>Tranzeo (PXP)</h3>
Wireless/Tranzeo/Tranzeo (PXP)|com.dartware.wrls.tranzeopxp.txt|05|<p>This probe is meant to probe a <a href="http://www.tranzeo.com">Tranzeo</a> 1000, 2000, 3000, 400, and 4000-series all in one device used as a PXP (bridge), or as an SAI (station) in router mode.</p>
Wireless/Tranzeo/Tranzeo (PXP)|com.dartware.wrls.tranzeopxp.txt|06|<p>The probe retrieves and displays a number of variables for basic, ethernet, wireless, and bridge information. It will go into alarm and warning states based on user-defined parameters for Received Signal level, Expected versus actual Station Channel, and incoming traffic on the radio interface, as well as into alarm when the wireless or ethernet links are reported down.</p>
Wireless/Tranzeo/Tranzeo (PXP)|com.dartware.wrls.tranzeopxp.txt|07|<p>Supported Models: TR-410, TR-420, TR-430, TR-440, TR-450, TR-4115, TR-4215, TR-4315, TR-4415, TR-4118, TR-4218, TR-4318, TR-4418, TR-4500, and TR-4519. Wireless/Tranzeo/Tranzeo (PXP)|com.dartware.wrls.tranzeopxp.txt|11|<p><i>High Traffic Bytes alarm</i>, <i>High Traffic Bytes warning</i> </p>
Wireless/Tranzeo/Tranzeo (PXP)|com.dartware.wrls.tranzeopxp.txt|12|<li> enter thresholds for <b>Warning</b> and <b>Alarm</b>.</li>
Wireless/Tranzeo/Tranzeo (PXP)|com.dartware.wrls.tranzeopxp.txt|13|<p><i>Expected Channel</i> - the number of the expected channel. </p>

Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|02|<blockquote>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|03|<h3>CCU</h3>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|05|<p>This probe monitors a WaveRider CCU (access point). It retrieves and displays a number of variables for basic, traffic, and wireless information. It will go into alarm and warning states based on user-defined parameters for radio frequency, percentage of payloads not needing a retry, percentage of payloads sent as broadcast, percentage of payloads discarded, percentage of payloads "Rx PER", percentage of payloads with HCRC errors, "Rx No-Match" errors, and high traffic incoming on the wireless interface. It will also go into an alarm based on the global status indicator.</p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|06|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|07|<p><i>Expected Frequency</i> - the expected frequencey </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|08|<p><i>No Retry percentage too low alarm</i>, <i>No Retry percentage low warning</i>, </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|09|<p><i>Broadcast percentage too high alarm</i>, <i>Broadcast percentage high warning</i>, </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|10|<p><i>Discard percentage too high alarm</i>, <i>Discard percentage high warning</i>, </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|11|<p><i>Rx PER percentage too high alarm</i>, <i>Rx PER percentage high warning</i>, </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|12|<p><i>HCRC percentage too high alarm</i>, <i>HCRC percentage high warning</i>, </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|13|<p><i>Rx No-Match too high alarm</i>, <i>Rx No-Match high warning</i>, </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|14|<p><i>High Traffic Bytes alarm</i>, <i>High Traffic Bytes warning</i> </p>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|15|<li> enter <b>Warning</b> and <b>Alarm</b> thresholds.</li>
Wireless/WaveRider/CCU|com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt|16|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">com.dartware.wrls.waveriderccu.txt</span><br />

Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|02|<blockquote>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|03|<h3>Victron UPS</h3>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|05|<p>This probe monitors important values in the Victron UPS.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|06|<p><b>B. Displayed Values</b></p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|07|<p><i>UPS</i>: battery status, battery remaining, low voltage warning</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|08|<p><i>Input Voltage</i>: Phase 1, 2, and 3</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|09|<p><i>Ouput Voltage</i>: Phase 1, 2, and 3</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|10|<p><i>Victron Alarm Points defined</i>: (three values)</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|11|<p><b>Parameters</b></p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|12|<p><i>UPS Battery Status - Alarm</i> - ALARM threshold for Battery Status.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|13|<li> If the value is 2, the UPS working normally.</li>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|14|<li> If the value is 1, the UPS is on bypass, the device enters Alarm state.</li>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|15|<p><i>UPS Battery Remaining - Warning</i> - WARNING threshold for the estimated battery time remaining. If the Battery Remaining is less than this threshold, the device is set to <b>Warning</b>.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|16|<p><i>UPS Battery low Voltage - Warning</i> - WARNING threshold for the min. battery voltage. If the Battery voltage is less than this threshold, the device is set to <b>Warning</b>.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|17|<p><i>Low Input Voltage line [1,2, or 3] - Alarm</i> - ALARM threshold for the mininmum specified input voltage on phase 1, 2, or 3. If the input voltage drops below this threshold, the device is set to <b>Alarm</b>.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|18|<p><i>Low Output Voltage line [1,2, or 3] - Alarm</i> - ALARM threshold for the mininmum specified output voltage on phase 1, 2, or 3. If the output voltage drops below this threshold, the device is set to <b>Alarm</b>.</p>
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|19|<p class="probeinfo">Filename: <span class="code">de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt</span><br />
Network Devices/UPS/Victron UPS|de.medianet.freinet.ups.victron.txt|20|Version:  <span class="code">3.1</span></p>
